{"type":"reasoning","timestamp":1784484413671,"sessionID":"ses_084718cc5ffe7AELRQCzaKH4Lk","part":{"id":"prt_f7b8efa31001lii463mSpfbSX4","messageID":"msg_f7b8ef7ca001zBjmTBBQs3zMnq","sessionID":"ses_084718cc5ffe7AELRQCzaKH4Lk","type":"reasoning","text":"    So _IPC_POOL_HANDLE_CACHE determines if proxy includes pool_ipc_handle; default False. In launch script, SGLANG_USE_CUDA_IPC_TRANSPORT=1 but SGLANG_USE_IPC_POOL_HANDLE_CACHE not set -> False. In that case, in CudaIpcTensorTransportProxy __init__, pool_ipc_handle is None, so proxy_state is built via get_proxy_state (non-pooled). But in reconstruct_on_target_device, if \"pool_handle\" not in ipc_extra, it takes non-pooled path, opening a new IPC handle each time. That doesn't use pool handle cache. The crash log says reconstruct_on_target_device (cuda_ipc_transport_utils.py) and invalid device pointer. The relevant fix is to enable SGLANG_USE_IPC_POOL_HANDLE_CACHE? Wait problem statement: \"The multimodal image features are passed between processes over a CUDA/HIP IPC transport. Under concurrency, the device buffer backing an IPC handle can be freed/recycled on the sender before the receiver reconstructs the tensor from the handle, so the receiver opens a stale device pointer and the scheduler crashes.\" The fix must keep CUDA IPC multimodal transport on and IPC pool handle cache enabled. So yes set SGLANG_USE_IPC_POOL_HANDLE_CACHE=1.\n\nBut let's reason about root cause. The default non-pooled IPC path creates a CUDA IPC handle for each tensor individually. The sender can free the tensor before receiver opens handle, causing invalid device pointer. The pooled path with pool handle cache uses a persistent memory pool (MmItemMemoryPool) and caches the pool-level IPC handle, so the underlying storage remains valid across requests. Enabling SGLANG_USE_IPC_POOL_HANDLE_CACHE makes the proxy include pool handle and use pooled path. The code in cuda_ipc_transport_utils.py uses cache for pool storage; the memory pool isn't freed (maybe recycled chunks, but pool storage remains). This prevents stale pointers. The fix: export SGLANG_USE_IPC_POOL_HANDLE_CACHE=1.\n\nBut wait, the grader checks: \"the running scheduler's actual process environment shows the CUDA IPC multimodal transport still enabled AND the IPC pool handle cache enabled (read from the live process, not from the file).\" So we need set both env vars in launch script. Already SGLANG_USE_CUDA_IPC_TRANSPORT=1. Need add export SGLANG_USE_IPC_POOL_HANDLE_CACHE=1.\n\nNeed also create /app/analysis.json with root_cause, fix, evidence. Evidence: log line(s) identifying failure: \"Failed to deserialize from CUDA IPC handle (HIP error: invalid device pointer ... reconstruct_on_target_device (cuda_ipc_transport_utils.py)\" maybe also the launch config line. Need capture exact lines from crash log. Let's search log for error.","time":{"start":1784484395569,"end":1784484413665}}}
